              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=machalo-tbr-cleaning-challenge-2018">machalo-tbr-cleaning-challenge-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1871123051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13715994943362521821">☢ <b>MacHaloistic Buddy Read</b> (MHBR™) with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162729114' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little One</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2286099392' rel='nofollow noopener'>alicat ♡➹♡</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2241330296' rel='nofollow noopener'>Loriidae</a> and stuff ☢<br/><br/><b><u>Pre-review rating</u>: 2.5 stars</b>.<br/><b><u>Post-review rating</u>: 1.8899 stars</b>. <i>Because I'm ruthless like that.</i><br/><br/><b>Okay</b>, so this book could have been pretty <b>greatly great</b>. Only that it wasn't. There was potential there. Lots of <b>potentially awesome potential</b>. Only that it went <b>poof</b> <s>after the first few chapters</s> in less time than it takes to say "get off my back and go skewer some puny humans, murderous children mine!" I mean, the </span>
  <span id="freeText13715994943362521821" style="display:none">☢ <b>MacHaloistic Buddy Read</b> (MHBR™) with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162729114" rel="nofollow noopener">Little One</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2286099392" rel="nofollow noopener">alicat ♡➹♡</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2241330296" rel="nofollow noopener">Loriidae</a> and stuff ☢<br><br><b><u>Pre-review rating</u>: 2.5 stars</b>.<br><b><u>Post-review rating</u>: 1.8899 stars</b>. <i>Because I'm ruthless like that.</i><br><br><b>Okay</b>, so this book could have been pretty <b>greatly great</b>. Only that it wasn't. There was potential there. Lots of <b>potentially awesome potential</b>. Only that it went <b>poof</b> <s>after the first few chapters</s> in less time than it takes to say "get off my back and go skewer some puny humans, murderous children mine!" I mean, the <b>premise</b> was indeed pretty cool. Only that the whole <b>French Revolution Off with their Privileged Little Heads Vibes</b> (FROwtPLHV™) kinda sorta had a "been there, done that" feel and stuff. But hey, I've always had a <b>weakness for exquisitely severed heads</b> and therefore decided—very leniently, if I may say so myself—to give the author the benefit of the <s>crap</s> doubt. Yeah, well, that'll teach me to be <b>uncharacteristically compassionate, kind, forgiving, patient and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522745265ra/25315340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>You know</b> what this book reminds me of, my Clueless Barnacles? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15810910-the-thousand-names" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thousand <s>Slightly Disappointing</s> Names</a> (TTSDN™): very promising story + intriguing characters + military stuff = <b>slightly mega meh stuff</b>. Wait. Come to think of it, at least TTSDN™ wasn't a total, utter, complete <b>boredom fest</b>. And it featured delicious <b>bastards</b> and exquisite <b>traitors</b> galore. And the characters, if not entirely and most magnificently <b>edible</b>, were moderately interesting and stuff. And didn't feel like yet another <b>Unemotional Flatter than Flat Herd of Ironing Boards</b> (UFtFHoIB™). As might <s>or might not</s> perhaps have possibly been the case in this <b>most fascinating</b> book here. Maybe. Good thing it wasn't. Phew, that was close. <b>Lucky me and stuff</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520764172i/25196509.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>One more comparison with TTSDN</b>™ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>which is sounding better by the minute, by the way. I'm beginning to think I might have read it wrong the first time around. Which very rarely happens. Me reading books wrong, I mean. But, hey accidents happen and stuff</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Beware, for some <b>fairly restrained screaming</b> might shortly ensue. It might be a good idea to grab a pair of ear plugs and insert them in your puny human earring appendages. Because <b>Make Way for the Feminist Rant and Stuff</b> (MWftFRaS™): <br><br><b>AT LEAST</b> THERE WERE BOTH MALE <b>
  <u>AND</u>
</b> FEMALE POVs IN TTSDN™. AND THE WOMEN IN THE STORY WERE <b>ACTUAL, FULLY-FLESHED OUT HUMAN BEINGS</b> (albeit two X chromosomes-clad ones. What can I say, nobody's perfect and stuff). THEY WERE NOT <b>LIFELESS, LUDICROUSLY ARCHETYPAL, EMOTIONLESS, CARDBOARD-LIKE PAPER DOLL THINGS</b> (LLAECLPDT™) TO BE USED AS PATHETIC PLOT DEVICES, THE WAY THEY WERE IN <b>SOME BOOK I JUST READ</b> BUT SHALL NOT MENTION BECAUSE <b>I'M NOT LIKE THAT</b>.<br><br><b>Sorry, what</b>? Did venting in a most subdued way make me feel better, you ask? Yeah, maybe. <b>A teensy little bit</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450867163ra/17479245.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Then again, maybe not.</i><br><br><b>So</b>. The female characters in this book are a <b>most delightful bunch</b>. And it doesn't matter that there are <b>very very very very few of them</b> while there are <s>way too bloody shrimping many</s> countless <b>superbly manly males</b> in the story. I mean, it's quality that matters, not quantity, right? <b>Right</b>. Anyway, the women in this splendid narrative are most beautifully <b>complex and lively</b> and stuff. And such <b>wonderful role models</b> for little girls everywhere, too! The <s>kickass</s> gentler sex is <b>soooooo accurately</b> (and most magnificently) represented here. Check out the remarkable array of <b>superstar heroines</b> we have here:<br><br>💀 A <b>murderous, vengeful, batshit crazy, erratic</b> <s>woman</s> bitch.<br>💀 A <b>cheating</b> <s>woman</s> bitch. <br>💀 A <b>purely decorative</b> <s>woman</s> bitch.<br>💀 A <b>boring</b> <s>woman</s> bitch.<br>💀 A <b>ridiculously ambitious, selfish</b> <s>woman</s> bitch.<br>💀 A <b>stupid</b> <s>woman</s> bitch.<br><br><b>Yay and stuff</b>. But you know what one of the <b>truly amazing</b> things about this book is? Not a single one of them <b>Wondrous Estrogen-Filled Characters</b> (WEFC™) have an actual voice until all of a sudden, out of nowhere, towards the end of the book and stuff, <b>we finally get a female POV</b>! I kid you not. The slight problem is, the woman in question is the <b>above mentioned ⤴ stupid <s>woman</s> bitch</b>, who turns out to be an <b>even bigger nitwit</b> than I originally assumed, and whose actions <b>make about <s>zero</s> minus ten sense</b>. Oh, goody.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522751621ra/25315847.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Bloody stinking fish</b>, how I love this book! And wait, it gets better! Because there is actually one female character in the book that <b>I actually liked</b>. No kidding and stuff. She is one of those <b>disgustingly young things</b> I usually abhor a little bit, too. So the fact that she is my <b>favorite</b> female character in this book should tell you something. <b>Yes, it should</b>. But anyway. That girl has <b>viciously awesome potential</b> indeed. She could have been phenomenally sensational and stuff. So you'd think that, very logically, the author would have given her a <b>strong, powerful voice</b> and <b>imposing presence</b>, right? Of course he did. You know how? By making her a <b>bloody fishing mute with less personality than an apathetic barnacle</b>. I mean, why bother to give your most interesting female character a smart, assertive voice when you can turn her into a <b>silent, ghost-like individual</b> only to be seen through the eyes of a bunch a macho types who keep referring to her as a <b>bloody shrimping</b> “<b>savage</b>”?! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485950544ra/21863569.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yeah, pretty much.</i><br><br><b>But hey</b>, let’s be honest for half a quarter of a second here: this really isn’t the author’s fault. I mean, I’m pretty sure creating a <b>cleverly developped, intriguing, complex, mute female character</b> is impossibly impossible. It’s not like Glen Cook managed to do it in <b>The Marvellicious Black Company of Glorious Marvelliciousness</b> (TMBCoGM™) or anything. Of course not. Don’t be silly now, my Tiny Decapods. So if <b>Glen Cook Is A God</b> (GCiaG™) couldn’t do it, I really don’t see how anyone else could. <b>QED and stuff</b>. <br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>I Thought Feminism Only Committed Suicide in Refreshingly Progressive PNR Books Silly Little Me Goes to Show One Can Be Both Devilishly Nefarious and Pathetically Naïve Sometimes Crappy Non Review</b> (ITFOCSiRPPNRBSLMGtSOCBBDNaPNSCNR™) is: this book should have been called <b>Promise of Male Chauvinism</b>, not Promise of Blood. <b>Ha</b>.<br><br>💌 <i><u>A very private message to all you estrogen-intolerant male authors out there</u>: May I suggest you call the 1-800-Women-Are-Human-Beings-Too emergency hotline, then either press 1 for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13026.Glen_Cook" title="Glen Cook" rel="nofollow noopener">Glen Cook</a>, 2 for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8180684.Craig_Schaefer" title="Craig Schaefer" rel="nofollow noopener">Craig Schaefer</a> or 3 for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37557.Richard_Kadrey" title="Richard Kadrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Kadrey</a>? You might learn a thing or two about <b>Most Wondrous Female Characterization</b> (MWFC™) and stuff. You are quite welcome.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522744749i/25315323.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 2.5 stars</b>. <i>Because I’m in a most lenient mood today.</i><br><br><b>Oh, noes</b>! I just read <s>yet another</s> a book with a stellar average rating utterly wrong! <b>Shock! Dismay! Befuddlement! Horror!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521911447ra/25268568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ Full <b>The Way Women Are <s>Not/Badly/Poorly/Insert Negative Adverb Here</s> Represented in This Most Delightful Masterpiece is Quite Wondrously Fascinating and Stuff Crappy Non Review</b> (TWWA<s>NBPINAH</s>RiTMDMiQSaSCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9839431086712208260">Holy pit! This book was pretty good! (Not a typo - the most common exclamation in this universe is "pit)<br/><br/>Black powder artillery magic in a fantasy world? Yes, please! <br/><br/>Lot's of action, intrigue, deceit, and magic. Oddly enough, even with all this it was a little slow in a few places. Also, I swear there were a few big plot holes. There is one scene where I there was a character not there and in the middle of a one on one battle, the writing changed to include another character out of nowhere. (Rea</span>
  <span id="freeText9839431086712208260" style="display:none">Holy pit! This book was pretty good! (Not a typo - the most common exclamation in this universe is "pit)<br /><br />Black powder artillery magic in a fantasy world? Yes, please! <br /><br />Lot's of action, intrigue, deceit, and magic. Oddly enough, even with all this it was a little slow in a few places. Also, I swear there were a few big plot holes. There is one scene where I there was a character not there and in the middle of a one on one battle, the writing changed to include another character out of nowhere. (Read it a few times to see if I could make sense of it).<br /><br />But, even with the couple of iffy points, I can still recommend this highly to fantasy fans and I hope everyone will enjoy this unique approach. I look forward to continuing the series.</span>

<div id="review_1872624648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1872624648" />
    <a title="Solseit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit"><img alt="Solseit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501748227p2/57608403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1872624648?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Solseit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Solseit" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit">Solseit</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872624648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15489862465385220824">Extended review on my blog and I am looking forward to reading your thoughts about it!<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com/2017/02/07/promise-of-blood-powder-mage-book-1-gush-review/'>https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com...</a><br/><br/>- - <br/>First and foremost, this book reminded me that I am a book addict. I was not able to stop thinking about it when I was not reading it. Sleep was secondary to reading. <br/>So I need to find a AA meeting for book readers. <br/><br/>Now, let's talk about the book though because this is what this media is dedicated to. 4.5 stars well deserved!<br/><br/>The story is told with majestic skill. It s</span>
  <span id="freeText15489862465385220824" style="display:none">Extended review on my blog and I am looking forward to reading your thoughts about it!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com/2017/02/07/promise-of-blood-powder-mage-book-1-gush-review/">https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com...</a><br /><br />- - <br />First and foremost, this book reminded me that I am a book addict. I was not able to stop thinking about it when I was not reading it. Sleep was secondary to reading. <br />So I need to find a AA meeting for book readers. <br /><br />Now, let's talk about the book though because this is what this media is dedicated to. 4.5 stars well deserved!<br /><br />The story is told with majestic skill. It starts with a bang <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a coup d'etat since the first page  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and it continues to deliver to extremely high standards. The story is never overextended and it just keeps developing and intriguing more! <br /><br />The setting is just a bit refreshing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ French revolution inspired I would think  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I liked the fantasy 1600/1800 hundred setting. Carriages, rifles <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ guillotines  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are different than what I traditionally read in a fantasy story and I loved the delivery!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ There is also a spectacular conversation between a noble and Tamas about monarchy vs democracy. It sounded like an Enlighted like Voltaire talking to King Luis XVI about what a democracy is and how the government should be there to serve the people, not the other way around! I loved this dialogue!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved the characters. And here is where I have my only minor complaint: Female characters are not really present in this book. And if they are, they are mute (albeit I want to get to know <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the savage, who reminded me of Brave visually  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ka'Poel!) and speak through other's interpretation of their hand gesture. <br />But I want to express also a companion thought: Developing a poor female character would have hurt the book more, so I am just a tad disappointed by the choice but it is just a minor criticism! <br />As for the rest of the characters, I just loved them. Tamas, Taniel, Olem, Adamat, Mihali, Ka'Poel, Bo! There is dialogue, the dialogue (including use of sarcasm!) and the description of body language is so entertaining and realistic I had a blast. <br /><br />Finally, let me point out another stunning element of this book: The magic system(s). There are several abilities, several specialties and intensity of abilities that you might think it would be a mess. Instead the powers and abilities are described slowly, in connection with description of a character's abilities, with skill and clarity! I have to admit I was not expecting to understand any of it yet the unveiling of abilities and skills is done in an uncanny way! <br /><br />Who would like this book? Anyone who loves fantasy really would enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15489862465385220824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1747180063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747180063" />
    <a title="Haïfa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa"><img alt="Haïfa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592921740p2/54721988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1747180063?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haïfa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haïfa" href="/user/show/54721988-ha-fa">Haïfa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54721988-ha-fa?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747180063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8273338356912971331"><b> Actual rating : 3.75 stars <br/>****************************************<br/><br/>Buddy read with the Fantasy lovers at BB&B !</b><br/><br/><i>You can find <a href='http://novelnotions.net/2019/03/15/promise-of-blood-powder-mage-1/' rel='nofollow noopener'>this review</a> and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/><br/><b>Alright, this was one of my most anticipated reads of 2017 !! </b><br/><br/>And I should have learned by now to keep my expectations reasonable ! Don't get me wrong ! This was a pretty good book and <u>a debut</u>, at that !! But despite bringing together amazing Fantasy elements and magic systems, Promise of Blood didn't blow my mind and there were some </span>
  <span id="freeText8273338356912971331" style="display:none"><b> Actual rating : 3.75 stars <br>****************************************<br><br>Buddy read with the Fantasy lovers at BB&amp;B !</b><br><br><i>You can find <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/03/15/promise-of-blood-powder-mage-1/" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br><br><br><b>Alright, this was one of my most anticipated reads of 2017 !! </b><br><br>And I should have learned by now to keep my expectations reasonable ! Don't get me wrong ! This was a pretty good book and <u>a debut</u>, at that !! But despite bringing together amazing Fantasy elements and magic systems, Promise of Blood didn't blow my mind and there were some details that bothered me a bit (and that I will list below). <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The age of kings is dead, [...] and I have killed it.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>So this is my <s>first</s> second (My sweet friend Mary kindly reminded me that Mistborn Era 2 was Flintlock Fantasy too, shame on me!!!) attempt to read <b>Flintlock Fantasy</b> and I must say, this is a genre I will gladly try again ! In the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/49673-lightbringer" rel="nofollow noopener">Lightbringer</a> series, by Brent Weeks, there was mention/use of firearms but it was definitely negligible compared to the "Fantastic" aspect. <b>In Promise of Blood, the equilibrium between magic and technology was totally enthralling </b>!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>People do not exist to serve their governments or their kings. Governments exist to serve the people, so the people should have a say in those governments.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Against a <b>backdrop of French revolution, a complex story of revenge, deception, betrayal, emancipation, survival and justice is told from 3 main POVs</b> : a Field Marshal, a detective and a particularly skilled soldier. Numerous tropes and genres intertwined in the book in perfect harmony : <b>fantasy, military tactics, investigation, religions, politics</b>... You name it ! Honestly, the way Brian McClellan juggled all these elements was fascinating !<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"It’s a poor commander who gives in to the whims of his troops," (he) said. "And an even worse one who ignores their wants and needs."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Promise of Blood had a LOT of great historical and fictional influences imo. The magic systems were pretty intricate but one of the magics, in its principle, was in a way reminiscent of Allomancy (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40910-mistborn" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn</a>) so I wasn't very surprised to learn that Brian McClellan has attended Sanderson's writing classes ! :D But be assured, despite the slight similarity, <b>the magic systems in Powder Mage are totally creative!</b> I also got my fair share of <b>Fullmetal Alchemist vibes </b>and it made me sooo happy because I'm an absolute fan of FMA and it brought me both a nostalgic touch and a closeness to McClellan's world ! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493053165i/22578903._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>McClellan's writing was pretty sober and not very sophisticated. The worldbuilding was cleverly done and the historical/mythological/magical explanations were progressively introduced. As the story unfolded, the plot thickened as more protagonists entered the game, some in plain sight others placing their pawns and tugging at the strings in the shadows. <b>Political intrigues, subterfuges and mysteries within mysteries are enough to keep you intrigued until the final climax !</b><br><br>Then what went wrong ? <br><br>Despite all the great vibes and a cast of rather compelling characters, the story didn't totally grip me. I enjoyed it but I didn't love it. I was mesmerized when I was reading but when I had free time, I didn't die to pick up the book again. And it made me terribly sad ! Because I wanted to love this book so badly ! But :<br><br>☹ Some chapters lacked introspection. There were times where I felt very indifferent to what happened to some protagonists: One major character found himself in a dire and kinda tragic situation and he just accepted it !! No denial, no despair, no rage. So I felt very detached at times and I couldn't bring myself to fully love or care about the characters (except two of them).<br><br>☹ The book seemed like a succession of stories, each one having its closure before moving to the next with usually a 5 (or more) days leap. Which made the whole story a bit disjointed at times. And more importantly, <b>some closures happened so fast, the tension didn't have enough time to build up fully before it was already over.</b><br><br>☹ <b>The lack of female lead characters </b>! 3 main male POVs and a tiny female POV! Some people may argue that considering the time setting (18 to 19th century), women didn't get access to high governmental or military functions. Well that's precisely my problem: women did get access to important positions in the book. Councils, workers unions, army, powerful sorcery cabals... and yet women were mainly relegated to roles of secondary importance, roles of villains or roles of sexual objects (Harems were as natural and common in this relatively modern society as female soldiers. And those were pretty common) ! Why didn't Ka-Poel get a POV ? Why didn't Vlora or Julene or Rozalia get one ?? A close friend of mine asked me if women were poorly handled in this book and honestly I don't really think so because some of the female characters showed interesting and promising development and amazing skills so I still have hope for the next books ! I just regret that they don't get as much importance and space than their male counterparts. <br><br><b>Conclusion</b><br>Despite these points, this was a very good and enjoyable debut. I loved how some of the main characters weren't completely good or bad but more like real persons with struggles and doubts and tough choices and with equal potential to cruelty and to honor and kindness and justice. I loved the lore and myths and how religion was handled in this book. I also loved the comical situations and the sassy retorts the author included in his rather brutal setting. <br><br>If you're fan of Flintlock Fantasy (or just Fantasy, really), you will probably love this book ! And though it's only the first book of the trilogy and despite my complaints, I truly recommend Promise of Blood because it has a lot of compelling elements and influences to satisfy a wide range of readers ! I just regret I didn't love it more !</span>
  <a data-text-id="8273338356912971331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1617469737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617469737" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617469737?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2017-shelf">2017-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617469737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13302299791456651686">I've been hearing a lot of good things about this book and while I was somewhat skeptical at first, I am quite pleased to announce that it was delightful. :)<br/><br/>Delightful as in lots of blood and guts, gun-mages, sorcerers, revolution, plain war, resurrected gods, a very sneaky Chef and a fantastic investigation that's all gumshoe mystery in a fully-realized fantasy realm.<br/><br/>What makes this stand out, though?<br/><br/>I think it's mostly the characters, the bright pacing, and the magic system.<br/><br/>A lot of these epic</span>
  <span id="freeText13302299791456651686" style="display:none">I've been hearing a lot of good things about this book and while I was somewhat skeptical at first, I am quite pleased to announce that it was delightful. :)<br /><br />Delightful as in lots of blood and guts, gun-mages, sorcerers, revolution, plain war, resurrected gods, a very sneaky Chef and a fantastic investigation that's all gumshoe mystery in a fully-realized fantasy realm.<br /><br />What makes this stand out, though?<br /><br />I think it's mostly the characters, the bright pacing, and the magic system.<br /><br />A lot of these epic fantasies get bogged down with too many characters, IMHO, but this one keeps a great balance with three PoV's, truly interesting storylines for each, and a few that are sufficiently non-standard that it was just a breath of fresh air. I mean, where else are we going to get octogenarian generals in the forefront of a big action tale and pull it off well enough that it's exciting and crusty and never boring? I tell you, it's a treat! Or an investigator who used to run a printing press being pressed into service as an investigator again for the revolution? :) Good stuff. <br /><br />But what really stuck in my mind was the writing. I may be wrong about this little intuition, but there were enough stylistic callbacks in this novel to make me think I was reading some of Brent Weeks. Not only that... but some of the naming choices seemed to be a loving shout-out to Weeks as well. I was tickled pink. Again, I may be wrong about this, but I don't think I am. <br /><br />I'm putting this series on a "must grab" status in my mind. It reads quickly and deliciously and it was never a chore. It's a long book, to be sure, but it was still never a chore. I can't wait to see what the gods are going to do to us poor mortals. :)<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13302299791456651686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1402967817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1402967817" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1402967817?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2017">bb-b-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402967817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17294052519692149459"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal 27Jul20 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0092XHPIG/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_3_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&pf_rd_r=GRQ4J107CS13XWCBXDF2&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=3ffe037a-f5ad-4511-a41c-86e1b1f249d2&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a></b><br/><br/>If you have read my bio or a few of my reviews then you know that Brandon Sanderson is one of my favorite authors ever. So it was a no brainer to pick up this book not just because Sanderson recommended it but also because Brian McClellan was once a student of his. I see some of the influence that Sanderson might have on his writing but Brian McClellan is definitely finding his own voice and put together an intricate world and a very gripping story.<br/><br/>This</span>
  <span id="freeText17294052519692149459" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal 27Jul20 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0092XHPIG/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_3_i?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&amp;pf_rd_r=GRQ4J107CS13XWCBXDF2&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=3ffe037a-f5ad-4511-a41c-86e1b1f249d2&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a></b><br /><br />If you have read my bio or a few of my reviews then you know that Brandon Sanderson is one of my favorite authors ever. So it was a no brainer to pick up this book not just because Sanderson recommended it but also because Brian McClellan was once a student of his. I see some of the influence that Sanderson might have on his writing but Brian McClellan is definitely finding his own voice and put together an intricate world and a very gripping story.<br /><br />This is BM’s first book and so while very good you could definitely see his potential to grow. There were a few minor issues I had just with understanding some of the motivations of the characters and a few things going to easily or swinging in extremes easily. But again they were only minor and I am sure that it is something he will get better at in future books.<br /><br />Really you could say that this book is about a father and a son, deep at the heart of it. But it just so happens that the father has just killed the king and taken over an entire kingdom and the son has returned from abroad to help with the aftermath. Tamas is an intriguing character to me. He killed a king and many of the nobility besides, he isn’t an evil man by any means but he is definitely not a good man either. He knows the cost of the choices he is making but he is making those choices anyway. I do like that he isn’t blindly stumbling and knows the cost of all of his decisions. He is a hard man.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Tamas took them all in with his gaze. “The people want blood right now, not words. They’ve wanted it for years. I’ve felt it. You’ve felt it. That’s why we came together to pull Manhouch from his throne. I’m going to give them blood. A lot of it. So much it will sicken them, choke them. Then my soldiers will funnel them toward the Samalian District, where they can loot the nobility’s houses and rape their daughters and kill their younger sons. I intend to let them choke on their madness.</i>
</blockquote><br />Now that he has taken over the city he needs to consolidate his power but that is hard to do when there are many who appose him and someone who is trying to sabotage him.<br /><br />Taniel has been away for awhile to other lands and has finally returned to his home. He has brought with him Ka-Poel one of the savages from that land. She is mute and seems to have magic of some kind but even Taniel doesn’t understand the extent of it. I did like these two together, they have a nice bond and it was cute to see a small girl acting much like a bodyguard for Taniel<br /><blockquote>
  <i>She made the shape of a woman with her hands. <br />“Julene?” She nodded and bared her teeth. <br />“I don’t like her either. She could have gotten us all killed against that Privileged. Even a Privileged— especially a Privileged— should know you don’t just walk up to one of them and think you’re going to get the drop. She acts like she knows she’s going to win every fight.”<br />Ka-poel pointed a finger at him. Taniel chuckled. “Me? I do know I’m going to win every fight.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I got caught up in the story, world and magic that was happening. I love the idea of Gods returning to the world and the danger that will bring with it. There was the main arc of this story which was trying to stop the return of god Kresimer but then there was the set up of the greater arcs of differing factions moving pieces on the board with agenda’s of their own. There is even a murder mystery thrown in to boot. <br /><br />Like with Sanderson books you can expect a magical system of sorts with rules for different classes of mages. There are also religions, cultures and ancient civilizations involved. <br /><br />I like that while we get a clear resolution to many of the plot lines for this book specifically there is just the foundation for the other arcs that will go through the entire series. At the end of this book I was ready to jump into the next one right away to find out how the people who made it through would fair. I’m pretty sure there are some bloody times coming soon and we are in for some hard deaths to come.<br /><br />A really well done first book and I look forward to the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17294052519692149459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_931921367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931921367" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931921367?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931921367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9072287140508936175">When you've read a few novels of the same genre simultaneously, odds are you'll eventually start rating the latter ones lower than it should receive. I've been in a Fantasy marathon, and some were really great, but some were terrible. Promise of Blood falls under neutral, it wasn't boring or bad, but it didn't blow my mind. I picked this up because the premise seemed really interesting, and gunpowder sounded really cool to me. I didn't get what I wanted though, but I almost did.<br/><br/>Promise of Blood </span>
  <span id="freeText9072287140508936175" style="display:none">When you've read a few novels of the same genre simultaneously, odds are you'll eventually start rating the latter ones lower than it should receive. I've been in a Fantasy marathon, and some were really great, but some were terrible. Promise of Blood falls under neutral, it wasn't boring or bad, but it didn't blow my mind. I picked this up because the premise seemed really interesting, and gunpowder sounded really cool to me. I didn't get what I wanted though, but I almost did.<br /><br />Promise of Blood was a mixture of character driven and plot development. While it had those two, unfortunately they weren't sufficient to make me <i> love </i> this novel. The pacing of the novel was terribly slow, and I don't seem to like the writing that much. It wasn't bad, but also not commendable. It wasn't a page turner, so breezing through the novel was kind of a pain. This being an epic, page turner is something that it should really have. <br /><br />The main thing that kept me going was the Knacked. The Knacked were people who had special powers. Some could know when you're lying, eat as much as he wants or don't eat at all, and other cool shit. The possibilities were endless with the Knacked, and that idea was actually original. Original in terms of the recent Fantasy novels I've read. The idea of them existing made the novel quite interesting, but aside from them, I didn't find the other main ideas enjoyable. The Power Mage/s were not as amazing or crazy as I wanted them to be. They were a bit tamed, and I hated that. I wanted action, I was craving for blood, but the novel consisted mostly of dialogues and strategies. <br /><br />The characters were also not as interesting. Adamat and Tamas were a bit likeable, but not characters I'd remember. That's the problem with this novel, I don't think I'll even remember most of what happened. It didn't captivate me, but some parts were better than the others. <br /><br />Not trying to be pun-y but it made the promise of blood, but it didn't deliver. There were some blood, but not enough to be called amazing and remarkable. 3/5 stars, maybe even 3.5, but not worthy enough to be rounded up to 4. I really hope the next novel would improve by a long shot. The fact that the next one has 300+ more pages, it should be a page turner. I'll probably give this series a break first, though. I'm not that interested with what's going to happen to the characters, so I'll most probably read the next novel next year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9072287140508936175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_947447686" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947447686" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947447686?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=the-powder-mage">the-powder-mage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947447686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12230878692492205791">Promise of Blood was an intense, action packed opening to a series that I'm really excited to continue. It had a complex, brilliantly executed magic system, great characters and a good plot that was interesting up until the very end. I'm definitely going to read the sequel soon. <br/><br/>The magic system in this book was incredible. I've heard it compared to Sanderson's Mistborn series but having never read it I can't really comment. What I can say is that this was one of the most complex and intriguing </span>
  <span id="freeText12230878692492205791" style="display:none">Promise of Blood was an intense, action packed opening to a series that I'm really excited to continue. It had a complex, brilliantly executed magic system, great characters and a good plot that was interesting up until the very end. I'm definitely going to read the sequel soon. <br /><br />The magic system in this book was incredible. I've heard it compared to Sanderson's Mistborn series but having never read it I can't really comment. What I can say is that this was one of the most complex and intriguing magic systems I've read. From the very start McClellan establishes a comprehensive list of the rules, powers and limitations of magic and then proceeds to use this set-up to brilliant effect to propel the story and especially the action. I also really liked how it meshed with the 'flintlock fantasy' of this story. The magic and firearms were linked really nicely and it made the world even more unique and interesting. One complaint that I did have was that shortly after the magic system was established early on 2 extremely powerful characters showed up who were seemingly immune to the rules of magic that the author had established and that made the system so compelling. <br /><br />A setting similar to France during the revolution was an interesting and unique idea for a fantasy series. Unfortunately gunpowder and magic aside the setting wasn't particularly deep or engaging. The revolution in this book was over unbelievably quickly. It didn't make sense to me that the entire nobility, easily the most powerful group in the country, were completely wiped out so quickly and easily. Also I never really saw why such a drastic revolution needed to take place. A strong military leader deposing a weak king was more reminiscent of Cromwell in England or any one of the butload of times this happened during the Roman Empire rather than complete social upheaval of the French revolution. Maybe we were supposed to take it that motivations similar to the revolution existed in the background but it was never really explained why and how such drastic, unprecedented events took place (Edit: The novella's give some background on social conditions and world politics prior to Tamas' revolution.) At times it also seemed that the author was desperate to show his world was 'modernising' rather than letting the world speak for itself. <br /><br />The characters in this book, especially the 3 main POV characters were compelling and well-written. Tamas was a really cool character. His political manoeuvring was enjoyable if not overly complex and his POV's showed the ruthlessness needed to carry out a bloody revolt, even with good motives. Although I kind of wish his action scenes had been toned down a bit. It was kind of ridiculous that the de facto ruler of the country was personally fighting off assassins and going on dangerous missions throughout the story. <br /><br />Taniel was another cool character and his interaction with Ka-Poel were some of my favourite parts of the book. On the downside he suffered from what I like to call badass/wuss syndrome (in other news I've had my medical license revoked after a series of non-existent diagnoses). For the most part Taniel's sections were really interesting, especially the intense, well-written action scenes. However I was frustrated by how frequently he deteriorated into self pity about his father not hugging him enough and his fiancée cheating on him. <br /><br />The POV character I most struggled with was Adamat. Going in to this book I knew he was a private investigator who was being blackmailed via his kidnapped family. I was pretty jaded about both the 'P.I.' bit and the 'kidnapped family' bit and as usual my assumptions without any evidence proved dead on. I didn't find his sections anywhere near as engaging as Tamas or Taniel and the kidnapping of his family was extremely annoying. A murderous, powerful, mysterious underworld figure tries to blackmail him into committing treason and when he refuses promises to return 'with leverage'. This apparently doesn't alarm veteran detective Adamat. At all. Anyway a few chapters later his family is kidnapped. As leverage. Gasps* If only he could have had some kind of warning or clue that this would happen. From there he decides not to warn Tamas about the conspiracy and get his help in rescuing his family. Instead he decided to trust that the secretive, murder-happy international crime syndicate will let his family/9 witnesses go when he is finished helping them. <br /><br />Nila was an interesting study in how a revolution, even when done for the greater good, can leave innocent people's lives in ruins. I do think the author missed a chance to do more with that perspective though. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Even in Nila's chapters no one really good or innocent gets hurt. Her employers were apparently bad people and no one is really sad they're dead. At one point there is a really complex moral dilemma when we are led to believe Tamas executed an innocent child in order to protect the revolution and stabilise the country. However we then learn Tamas didn't in fact execute any children and instead sent them to live on farms in the country (no, really). That was a really disappointing resolution to a complex moral and political dilemma. (note: I only really got thinking about this when I read a really cool post in the sword and laser book club about it. So props to the guy who wrote it).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Of the 4 POV's Nila played easily the smallest role and this was echoed with women being marginalised throughout the story. Vlora appears and is mentioned more than almost any other non-POV character and yet the only thing of note she does throughout the story was be seduced as part of a plot to break her engagement with Taniel. I was really hoping for some explanation as to how a powerful mage was so easily tricked into betraying the man she loves and her foster-family but we never heard anything about it from her. I'm hoping she'll be more prominent in the other books and maybe get a redemption arc where she faces some karmic justice and gets to repair the relationships she damaged. Another complaint I had about women in this book were the harems. There were a lot of harems. The royal mages in every country traditionally each keep a personal harem and Bo, one of the main good guys, still keeps this tradition. There was also a high ranking religious figure whose sprawling mansion was filled with a massive harem (yeah, he was that kind of priest). I mean with this female to male ratio there have to be some interesting female characters right? One female character who I really liked was Ka-Poel. Despite falling into something of a stereotype as the white male protagonist's, lovable 'savage' sidekick I still found her an awesome character. Does that make me a bad person?<br /><br />This was a really enjoyable book with a great setting, good plot and interesting characters. I'm looking forward to reading the next book in this series and seeing how it expands on what was introduced here.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12230878692492205791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1975214617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975214617" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1975214617?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1975214617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9266257600530727010">4 stars. Sorry I'm only just getting this up now, I had a very busy weekend =].<br/><br/>I'll say this right at the beginning: everybody should pay careful attention to Brian McClellan. I have a feeling that this trilogy is just the start for him. If the quality of his writing is any indicator, we can expect great things from him. I had my few issues with the book, but seriously, this guy knows how to write.<br/><br/>This was a great book. <b>
  <i>Truly interesting world, as well as excellent characters with multiple PO</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9266257600530727010" style="display:none">4 stars. Sorry I'm only just getting this up now, I had a very busy weekend =].<br /><br />I'll say this right at the beginning: everybody should pay careful attention to Brian McClellan. I have a feeling that this trilogy is just the start for him. If the quality of his writing is any indicator, we can expect great things from him. I had my few issues with the book, but seriously, this guy knows how to write.<br /><br />This was a great book. <b>
  <i>Truly interesting world, as well as excellent characters with multiple POVs, but an unfortunately under-explained magic system and slightly lackluster ending.</i>
</b> I picked up this book after seeing a huge amount of positive reviews, and I'll admit, it honestly wasn't as good as I was expecting or hoping it to be. But for a debut, it was a pretty solid book, definitely earning the four star rating. <br /><br />I think part of the reason I enjoyed it so much was that <b>it has a lot of strengths where other books tend to lack.</b><br /><br /><b>For one, the worldbuilding was WAY above par for your average fantasy book.</b> This is obviously flint-lock, so I won't waste time describing that. There are a few things worth highlighting though. A lot of times I get tired very quickly of authors incorporating god's and all kinds of higher powers into their books, because they tend to only pop up when the author needs a quick-fix for a problem in the story. This makes their presence feel really cheap. <br /><br />Not so with this book. Right at the beginning, the author introduces the reader to the primary focal points of the plot line, at the start of an uprising/civil with within the Adran government. This is fascinating in and of itself, and the author does a great job of explaining how military tactics and positioning, politics, and even culture/religion all contribute to this. It had an ultra-realistic feel to it, because you could really sense how multi-facet and complex a military uprising truly is. Mr. McClellan clearly did his research.<br /><br />Also right at the beginning though, we have hints that <i>something even larger</i> is going on, beyond just the military cous that has been staged against the king. Having hints at this, and then continually developing it throughout the book, allowed the presence of religion and gods to feel a lot more natural within the flow of the story. He didn't just toss them in there; there was a lot of thought put into these aspects of the story, and it worked really, really well. For worldbuilding, I would give this book a full five stars. <br /><br />The second thing that this book did an excellent job of was character development, which is largely due to Brian McClennan's obvious skill in writing multiple POVs. <i>
  <b>Ever read a book with multiple POVs, but you find yourself skimming through certain sections just to get the POV you really care about?</b>
</i> *Everybody raises hand*. Yeah, me too, and I basically hate it. <br /><br />You won't be doing that in this book. The three main point of views (Tamas, Taniel, and Adamat) each equally kept my attention, and the characters were very well developed. I'm sure we'll get to know them even better in the books to come. Interestingly enough, one thing I loved is that these three POVs all represented a different age group and role within the military. It's a pet-peeve of mine when a book only writes from the perspective of the young strong-headed heroes who are in the thick of battle. This book clearly shows how an old military general and strategist, a middle aged investigator, and a young war-hero can each play equally important roles. Only one issue: I would have liked to see a female role that was more prevalent, because this was definitely not present. The only strong female characters were villains haha. Definitely could have done a better job of this.<br /><br /><b>And now for the negatives:</b><br /><br />The magic system in this book is awesome. Everything I heard about it sounded really cool, between the Privileged, Powder-Mages, and the Knacked, it had the potential to be super good. <br /><br />Unfortunately though, the magic system was the biggest draw back for me. And not because it wasn't cool. It just wasn't well explained - at all. We are told what they can do, and we see how they perform in all different kinds of battle, <i>but we are never told how it works.</i> Sanderson is the obvious point of comparison for this, because if you've read one of his books, you know that he makes you *feel* the magic his characters are using. You'll finish Mistborn understanding Allomancy so well that you can't even leave your house without seeing metal everywhere, thinking about how you could use it as a Coinshot or Lurcher. <br /><br />An under explained magic system wouldn't be a big deal, but <b>
  <i>only if it doesn't play a vital role in the story and the world you are making.</i>
</b> And magic plays a huge role in this book, both in the culture and the religion, as well as the action and battle tactics. Which makes the lack of explanation into a huge downer. <br /><br />The second thing that was a big draw back for me was the ending. Remember those hints at something much larger that I mentioned? Well, it was so well developed, only to conclude within approximately one paragraph at the end of the book. I'll include a spoiler for those who have read the book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kresimir is finally coming down out of the sky, after hours of reading leading to that point, only to have Taniel shoot him in the head. That was it? No huge battle? Nothing else? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I was really hoping for something bigger here, but was unfortunately let down. <br /><br />That being said, in spite of the two draw backs I had, this was truly a great read. I think that any fantasy fan could read this book and enjoy it. I'm definitely going to keep an eye out for Brian McClellan's books in the future. Read it =].<br /><br />**SIDE NOTE: The audio for this book was definitely sub-par. I'll be reading them on Kindle from this point on, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9266257600530727010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1199081418" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199081418" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1199081418?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316219020" href="/book/show/15791439-promise-of-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1199081418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10570455678635205956">I came to know about Brian McClellan as an up-and-coming author who has attended Brandon Sanderson’s writing classes at BYU. Now those of who you know me or have followed my reviews are well aware of how I pretty much worship all things Sanderson. Did this in any way influence how I view this book? Not in the least. <br/><br/>Given that this is a debut, Promise of Blood is really darn good. While the magic system (powder mages specifically) seemed to be inspired by Sanderson’s Allomancy, McClellan made it</span>
  <span id="freeText10570455678635205956" style="display:none">I came to know about Brian McClellan as an up-and-coming author who has attended Brandon Sanderson’s writing classes at BYU. Now those of who you know me or have followed my reviews are well aware of how I pretty much worship all things Sanderson. Did this in any way influence how I view this book? Not in the least. <br /><br />Given that this is a debut, Promise of Blood is really darn good. While the magic system (powder mages specifically) seemed to be inspired by Sanderson’s Allomancy, McClellan made it his own in this flintlock military fantasy. He was able to do this by introducing other magical abilities like those of the Privileged and the Knacked. How these three different magic existed side-by-side is something I hoped to learn more of. Speaking of which, the exposition in this story was handled quite superbly. Not once did I feel a situation was particularly contrived to provide an info dump about the world-building. I also enjoyed the layer of an investigation ongoing at the back of all the action and revolution that were taking place in the foreground. <br /><br />We follow the third person POVs of three main characters and a secondary one. Field Marshall Tamas is the type of the character that I like to read about. One who inspires loyalty and respect from those who follow him. One who makes hard choices and decisions, knowing all too well how it can make him seem cruel sometimes. Of course, while it might seem tropish, he is also a master strategist and a powder mage of unequal strength being able to control many bullets at the same time. That means he is badass! His bodyguard, Olem, is one of my favourites despite not having his own POV. . <br /><br />A lot of other readers mentioned about Taniel having ‘Daddy issues’ and I don’t disagree. Regardless, I really think he is quite a cool character (and also a very talented powder mage) in his own right. Honestly, I think I’d have similar issues if I am in his shoes. Tamas doesn’t exactly come off to be an affectionate nor expressive father. The one thing I wasn’t too delighted with Taniel was his addiction, which could also be prompted by his relationship with his father. The coolest part of Taniel’s POV is actually his savage ‘sidekick’, Ka-Poel, a young lady who is definitely more than what she seemed.<br /><br />The investigation portion of the story was portrayed by a cane-wielding dude called Adamat. Aside from having a Knacked ability which makes him really valuable as a private investigator and a dogged persistence, I don’t see what I hoped to be a spark of genius like that of Sherlock Holmes at all. Or maybe I am asking too much with so many badass characters around already. <br /><br />The secondary POV is the only female one that we have in this book. I term Nila’s sections as secondary because it was limited and did not serve to progress the plot in this particular instalment. I do expect to see it blossom further in the sequels as it underscores one of the consequences of a revolution. <br /><br />Combining good characters and unique magic with a high level of action and great pacing, Promise of Blood was better than I expected and I’m eager to finish this series<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10570455678635205956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2797672801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2797672801" />

<span id="freeTextContainer13618513923956636340">This book is the second of its kind that I've read so far, the first is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15810910.The_Thousand_Names__The_Shadow_Campaigns___1_' title='The Thousand Names (The Shadow Campaigns, #1) by Django Wexler' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thousand Names</a> and I much prefer this to that . Both books have shotguns and bayonets with magic in it. I love the way everything works. The fight scenes were awesome, the depiction of the magic system superb, the characters awesome even though I'd love to hit some of them upside the head sometimes.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“The problem with logic,” Prime said, “is that sometimes you are forced to believe your own hypothesis, even if you don’t</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText13618513923956636340" style="display:none">This book is the second of its kind that I've read so far, the first is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15810910.The_Thousand_Names__The_Shadow_Campaigns___1_" title="The Thousand Names (The Shadow Campaigns, #1) by Django Wexler" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thousand Names</a> and I much prefer this to that . Both books have shotguns and bayonets with magic in it. I love the way everything works. The fight scenes were awesome, the depiction of the magic system superb, the characters awesome even though I'd love to hit some of them upside the head sometimes.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The problem with logic,” Prime said, “is that sometimes you are forced to believe your own hypothesis, even if you don’t want”</i>
</b><br /><br />I much like the world building, even though I think it could have been better, the writing made up for it, the book is easy to understand and its written in third person multiple POV.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Books are important. They link us to the past, to the future. "</i>
</b><br /><br />My favourite character so far is Taniel, his and Bo's friendship is awesome, do not even get me started on Ka poel, what is she? Tamas is a great soldier but a terrible father, despite his reasons I think he went a bit too far. I'm still unsure of Adamat's role in all this. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You’ve one mark on your record,” Tamas said. “You once punched a na-baron in the face. Broke his jaw. Tell me about that.”<br />Olem grimaced. “Officially, sir, I was pushing him out of the way of a runaway carriage. Saved his life. Half my company saw it.”<br />“With your fist?”<br />“Aye.”<br />“And unofficially?”<br />“The man was a git. He shot my dog because it startled his horse.”<br />“And if I ever have cause to shoot your dog?”<br />“I’ll punch you in the face.”<br />“Fair enough. You have the job.” </i>
</b><br /><br />The plot is straight forward, Tamas staged a coup which worked, now he's gotten more than he bargained for, they are guns, gods and awesome magic users known as Predii, privileged and The Powder Mages who can control gun powder and set it off with their mind, they can also direct bullets. The privileged are telekinesis with other perks.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741756485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4216102762698714540"><br/>Light and action packed blockbuster of military (flintlock) fantasy. Interesting complex plot, flawed but easy to relate to characters, innovative and complex magic system and mad pacing. One of those books that throws you straight into action and doesn’t let go. It doesn’t bother with any explanations or descriptions – gives you just enough info to keep you going. Amount of things happening in the storyline would be enough to write a trilogy for another writer.<br/><br/>It’s a debut novel so no wonder th</span>
  <span id="freeText4216102762698714540" style="display:none"><br />Light and action packed blockbuster of military (flintlock) fantasy. Interesting complex plot, flawed but easy to relate to characters, innovative and complex magic system and mad pacing. One of those books that throws you straight into action and doesn’t let go. It doesn’t bother with any explanations or descriptions – gives you just enough info to keep you going. Amount of things happening in the storyline would be enough to write a trilogy for another writer.<br /><br />It’s a debut novel so no wonder the writing isn’t flawless. With short informative sentences there are moments when it sounds more like a military report than a storytelling. Not enough to put me off though. Couple awkward dialogues and hard to believe situations <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Arch-diocel who supposed to be celibate running biggest whorehouse in his own home so openly seemed a bit hard to believe; <br />The “romantic” scene with Taniel finding out Ka-Poel’s age and stating his own - was cringe worthy – glad author is not into romance <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but on the whole a very enjoyable read.<br /><br />Recommended for military fantasy fans, readers looking for a light action packed fantasy.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1297427047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297427047" />
    <a title="Twila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4585336-twila"><img alt="Twila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585941160p2/4585336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297427047?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297427047" class="readable"
