<span id="freeTextContainer5139695168095227521"><i>“What must be done will be done.”</i><br/><br/><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I tried hard to convince myself to give <i>Promise of Blood</i> the complete 4 stars I wanted to give it. I have no negative feelings toward this book and I’m actually extremely fond of it, but after thinking about it and weighing all the pros and cons, I just couldn’t. I feel sort of bad about this because I really did enjoy the book, but like Sabon said, you do what you gotta do. I’m still a little upset with myself though ☹ <br/><br/><b>Alright, so this bo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5139695168095227521" style="display:none"><i>“What must be done will be done.”</i><br><br><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br><br>I tried hard to convince myself to give <i>Promise of Blood</i> the complete 4 stars I wanted to give it. I have no negative feelings toward this book and I’m actually extremely fond of it, but after thinking about it and weighing all the pros and cons, I just couldn’t. I feel sort of bad about this because I really did enjoy the book, but like Sabon said, you do what you gotta do. I’m still a little upset with myself though ☹ <br><br><b>Alright, so this book. There’s muskets, war, political intrigue, bayonet charges, magic, gods, and oh my!</b> This is only my third Flintlock Fantasy, but I absolutely adore the genre and I will never understand people who say guns and magic shouldn’t go together. IT WORKS SO WELL, leave it alone. It’s fun!<br><br>I am a person who doesn’t care too much for world-building, but it’s this book’s world that I think I enjoyed the most! <b>The idea of an industrial revolution taking place in magical world absolutely fascinates me.</b> The time period is something akin to our French Revolution, and I feel like the author took a lot of inspiration from that entire era, especially when the King gets booted off the throne in the very start of the book. <br><br>There are three tiers of sorcery: the Privileged, the Knacked, and the Marked/Powder Mage. I initially felt the magic highly improbable and extremely random, but it grew on me more and more as I kept reading. I especially like the concept of the Powder Mage because it reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68428.The_Final_Empire__Mistborn___1_" title="The Final Empire (Mistborn, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn's</a> <i>allomancy</i>, by my favourite author, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a>. <b>There’s a much higher degree of simplicity to the magic in this novel than Sanderson’s, but no matter, I still found it interesting and highly exciting.</b> But as far as I’m concerned, Brian McClellan still has some ways to go before his work is as polished as Sanderson’s. <br><br>I feel it a little unfair of me to keep comparing him to King Sanderson, but Mr. McClellan was his student once and I can’t help it. But still, <b>King stays King!</b> <br><br>This book has multiple stories going on at once. There’s Field Marshal Tamas who’s dealing all the fallout from the coup. His son, Taniel, is searching for a rogue Privileged. There’s inspector Adamat who is, well, <i>inspecting</i> things for Tamas. And there’s also the washer woman Nila, whose POV is only on the side. <br><br>There are a lot of characters, but McClellan has a knack [lol] for narrating this complex story and creating seamless—mostly—transitions between them, presenting it in such a way that makes it all very easy to follow. <br><br>But this is where my problems begin. <br><br><b>The character development is SOOOOO THIN</b> ☹ <br><br>I GENUINELY like most of these characters, but I didn’t find any of them to be particularly memorable. My favourite is Olem, and he unfortunately only has a supporting role. Next is Ka-poel, who has a larger role, but so much of her is unknown and shrouded in mystery. She’s an interesting counterpoint to Taniel, who is also great. I just need MORE. <b>All their motives were just so largely plain and clear from the get-go. They always did what I expected them to do, and I would have liked if they showed a little more complexity.</b><br><br>Tamas is the only character I found slightly memorable. He has an interesting dichotomy of having good intentions, but also being very brutal. There are not many “heroes” who literally answer to no one and Tamas is one of them, so I found him interesting to follow. He also really loves dogs, like me, and I found that to be such a sweet touch to the book. <br><br>I still can’t get over that he’s in his 60s by the way! <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494197176i/22692864._SX540_.png" width="400" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>C’mon, look at him. 55 at the most! <br><br>But anyway, maybe the problem for the character issue is that there are simply too many characters. To me, <b>Nila’s entire story arc could have been deleted and the heart of the book would remain completely the same</b>. So why was she in it??? <br><br>But again, I still really liked the characters and they totally entertained me, so it’s not a HUGE problem. But still a problem. <br><br>Alright, last thing. The pacing of the novel is extremely rough around the edges. It is SO uneven. After the initial coup, the story splits off into its different directions, and each storyline has a different pace. Taniel’s chapters were my favourites because that is where most of the action is. Adamat and Nila’s chapters were a complete drag to read and Tamas is somewhere in the middle. <br><br><b>Some parts felt rushed, others felt drawn-out, and some didn’t have any sort of tension at all.</b> The transitions between a fast-paced Taniel chapter to a slow-paced Adamat chapter slightly ruined things for me. I struggle through slow sections somewhat harder than most people because I’m actually attention deficit. And though I felt it highly exciting when McClellan would frequently jump on the throttle, the slow bits just left me disengaged and bored, spoiling the mood ☹<br><br><b>Aside from these blips, <i>Promise of Blood</i> is set in a wonderfully imagined world and is quite good for a debut.</b> There are bad guys of both regular and supernatural caliber that attack from all sides, making the novel hard to predict. And I’ll give bonus points for its quick start. It’s a rare book that wastes absolutely no time in getting the plot moving like this one does.<br><br>If I had to describe the book in one word, it is: <i>promising</i>.<br>*cringe*<br><br>Definitely excited to carry on with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5139695168095227521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8282711525230172319" style="display:none">This book was fantastic - best book I've read this year and I can't wait to read the rest (right after I finish the new Darker Shade of Magic book). I loved the characters, I loved the story line, and I liked the innovative idea that magic and guns could be used together. <br /><br />So one thing that has me a bit worried. I looked at the author's Goodread page and compared my books to his - I noticed he's read the Malazan books (which are huge favorites of mine), but then I noticed a disturbing similarity - this spoiler is for the Promise of Blood and the 1st three Malazan books - so fair warning - it will spoil Memories of Ice <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ so Tamas breaks his leg, and at the end of the book it's constantly mentioned how he has injured it, but hasn't taken the time to get the magical healer to fix it for him. <div id="review_1965862713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1965862713" />
    <a title="Skylar Phelps" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41541918-skylar-phelps"><img alt="Skylar Phelps" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575827186p2/41541918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1965862713?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skylar Phelps" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skylar Phelps" href="/user/show/41541918-skylar-phelps">Skylar Phelps</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1965862713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17022169625320932677">Going into Promise of Blood, I was a little hesitant for a couple of reasons. First of all, there are so many raving reviews, many of which from friends that I look up to and hold in respect as having excellent bookish taste. That’s not necessarily a bad thing but I worry that my expectations tend to put a damper on my actual experience and I never want to begin a book with preconceived judgments and/or presumptions.<br/><br/>Secondly, I quite recently completed the other front running flintlock fantasy s</span>
  <span id="freeText17022169625320932677" style="display:none">Going into Promise of Blood, I was a little hesitant for a couple of reasons. First of all, there are so many raving reviews, many of which from friends that I look up to and hold in respect as having excellent bookish taste. That’s not necessarily a bad thing but I worry that my expectations tend to put a damper on my actual experience and I never want to begin a book with preconceived judgments and/or presumptions.<br /><br />Secondly, I quite recently completed the other front running flintlock fantasy series by Django Wexler, which I enjoyed very much! I knew I would be comparing the two from the get-go even if only unintentionally.<br /><br />Well, I am thrilled to report that neither of those concerns conflicted me this go around! Promise of Blood was so much different than I expected, and I mean that in a fantastically satisfying way. It was exciting, intense and chalk full of intrigue. The two greatest strengths, imo, were the cast of awesome characters and the engaging plot progression. There really was never a dull moment between the militaristic banter and political chicanery; or between the memorable battle scenes and the overarching mysteries. <br /><br />With a start like this, the series shows promise to become a prized collection in my own personal library :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17022169625320932677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>
          <a title="Fantasy Buddy Reads" class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19201716-promise-of-blood-mar-15-2018">Fantasy Buddy Reads:</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JYuBu1jtmX6tW2l0fsPgVUX9Fa4j8lfN7VvIYGzGSEVoBu9lXsWoOG4YF+yFbB9liU+Y75XA7nxaPp49ybixLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ulumj44dGL2DlFtg5IMJTrvyQnd1uvYDppsRa1431OQf1shRiDUp+0DXJfgfLPZ+d0DPNsOIT7IR/kc2+0ktjA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText9023947907005203276" style="display:none">Brian McClellan is an American epic fantasy author from Cleveland, Ohio.
